<UserId.>111145018034016251926</UserId.>< Name>
Phil Davis< /Name>
<Time>1545810837507< /Time><Rate>4<//Rate>< Text>
I love having this donut shop in my neighborhood.

The donuts are great. The coffee is strong and fresh. Their bagel/croissant breakfast sandwiches are fantastic. Prices are reasonable. Parking is easy. We haven't tried their ice cream, boba, lunch sandwiches, or other offerings.

The folks behind the counter (Mom/Dad/Son?) are almost always friendly, helpful, and patient. Often we're surprised by extra donut holes or even a bonus donut later in the day. Very rarely they might have an off day or a really big crush of customers. The shop is not spotless and new. I don't mind. They're human. I like buying donuts from humans. If I wanted a standard, anonymous, corporate transaction, I'd go to Krispy Kreme, Safeway's bakery, or Starbucks for a scone.

Tips from my experience:

* For the best donut selection, get there before 9am. This is pretty standard for small donut shops. They usually have good donuts all day, but if you have your heart set on something specific like their apple fritters or a maple-glazed old fashioned, get there early.
* Their egg/bacon/cheese on the jalape√±o bagel is amazing. The individual ingredients are simple, but together they are just so satisfying. My family fights over the last jalape√±o bagel. If you want the jalape√±o bagel experience, get there early. 8am often means getting the last one.<//Text>

< review>
It has been a few months since I moved into AVA Toluca Hills and I could not be any happier. It‚Äôs a well-maintained community with gorgeous landscapes and rich nature all around, as well as exceptional amenities, including a convenience store, Amazon lockers for secure delivery, multiple gyms, swimming pools, tennis, basketball, volleyball courts, parks for pets, etc. Located no further than 10 minutes away from Hollywood or Burbank, it feels very soothing and more private than most apartment complexes in Los Angeles. These apartments have been a known spot for many creatives such as myself, who work in the animation, film, or music industries. -One or more of the amenities (pool etc...) being shut down for days at a time.

There are large stretches of street between building that have no side walks, so good luck trying to stick to the shoulder and not get hit by someone blowing around the curves at 40+mph.

All the units are in giant connected hallways that amplify ALL SOUNDS, and the walls are paper thin so you can hear almost all your neighbors at all times.

There is dog poop/ trash everywhere and no enforcement for picking it up, and the laundry room floors are covered in water.

Parking is a nightmare! And they recently got rid of a ton of free spaces and replaced them with reserved spaces that cost a ridiculous amount. So be prepared for a ten minute (no exaggeration) hike to and from your car.

The amenities are decent so I'll give one star for that, and the staff is pretty nice. Maintenance team is good too.

DONT LIVE HERE!</Text>

IT IS ALMOST IMPOSSIBLE TO FIND PARKING AFTER 10PM.

<text>- I currently live here, and I enjoy this complex; there are some great amenities like free parking (you can pay $60/month to have your own spot), pools, spas/hot tubs, gyms (albeit with no free weights), and several party rooms available for rent (like a small ballroom with bar, and a rehearsal room, and a small theater room). The location is also great, you are halfway to West Hollywood and to Burbank. The view is also pretty amazing depending on where you are, you can see Hogwarts and WB Studios if you are in the right area.
The drawbacks I have personally had are:
- 1) Quite a few spiders and insects (although there is plenty of vegetation around, so it's to be expected)
- 2) The appliances need updating
- 3) Some of the screens and windows could do with replacing/updating
- 4) Minor cracks and scrapes on the mirrors in bathrooms and bedrooms
- 5) I found pumpkin seeds and pieces of walnuts (that's just asking for rodents) in one of my cabinets and they were just painted over, not even thrown away, just painted over (also some of the paint is chipping in a few areas).
- 6) Some of the residents can be rude and very loud, it can be quite inconsiderate sometimes, early in the morning or late at night when quiet hours are supposed to be happening, they are NOT happening.
- I love this complex, but if I am paying a premium price, I would expect premium appliances, services, and apartments, NOT average or sub-par.
- Also, the carpet in walkways outside the apartments could do with replacing, some of the stains look a little unsightly; still I'd rather live here than the other places I have lived. Overall, if they fix these problems it would be a complete 5-Star Experience all around!
This review is mine, as well as on behalf of my roommates.</text><rating>3< /rating></record>

<date>1499547225027< /date>< Review>
Okay let's talk about this...

I've lived at this location for 3+ years. Moved in when it was Oakwood. Oakwood was great, there were some things that definitely needed some refreshing but for the most part the property was comfortable and felt like home.

However... this changed once Avalon took over...

If you read my earlier reviews you'll see that I've tried giving Avalon a fair chance... but unfortunately, this new construction taking place and the issues surrounding it are just a bit much now.

I've spoken with management quite a few times regarding my concerns but it has been to little avail each time and has generally been a waste of time.  Hence this updated review...

- Construction -

This is huge. Watch the NBC story online that covers the issues. 8am jackhammers, asbestos in the air, uninhabitable rooms and more. Avalon says that these updates are "necessary", however, there is NOTHING necessary about removing popcorn ceilings other than for aesthetics. The only necessary updates that I know of, would be in regards to the water piping which has had issues in the past.

Like many of the other posters, I was under the impression Avalon would only be updating unoccupied rooms and renovating rooms as tenants moved out... But alas, we were wrong.

Avalon actually thinks it's okay to kick us (and our pets) out of our rooms 8am-4pm, dismantle our living conditions and charge us the same amount of rent during the process. No discounts for living in a full-on construction site. Not to mention, they'll be increasing the rent on our rent controlled apartment by as much as 10% once the work is completed.

View the news story, and you will see just how unlivable and unbelievable this situation is. If you like living in a ziplock bag then this might be the place for you otherwise... I'd avoid it.

Also... apart from the noise and ridiculous conditions, I'd also like to point out that construction continually leaves large amounts of trash throughout the complex. Most of which is trash from their lunch break. My girlfriend has also had multiple issues with construction workers cat-calling her as she walks to her vehicle... Home sweet home, right?

- South Clubhouse Pool Closure -

This is a big one as well. There are two pools on this property. However, both pools get HEAVILY populated during the summer and on warm days. By some twisted logic, Avalon thought construction on the pool should start at the beginning of June for an 8 month overhaul. Why they couldn't wait until the end of summer is beyond me. Combine this with the south club house fitness center closure, and it's been a giant nuisance that could have been avoided.

- Security -

Many of the previous issues of security seem to have been addressed (like people being shot in the garage). However, I've had to report numerous noise complaints due to blaring music at 2am and it sometimes takes as many as 4 calls to security (over the course of an hour) until they are actually able to get it resolved.

- Aesthetic -

With dark grey exteriors and dilapidated living conditions, this place resembles more of a prison then a home. When you pull in to Avalon, make sure to spot the giant tombstone (complete with memorial flowers) by the temporary leasing office. It will point you in the direction of where you need to go.

- Conclusion -

* As far as location and maintenance go I still think the location is great and the maintenance team is fantastic. Likewise, I've had really great encounters with staff in the office.

I think the issues lie with the individuals further up the corporate ladder that are making the executive decisions.

These executives at Avalon could learn a lot by listening to the tenants. I understand this is a business for them but it is our lives they are seriously affecting.

We, as paying renters, deserve the right to live healthy and comfortably in our homes.<//Review>

<review>If I have to rate the place and apartment, I rate 5 stars. But if I have to rate Avalon management, definitely 1 star.

I lived in Oakwood Toluca hills for a total of 2.5 years now, on and off and until Avalon took the lead, everything was not great, was AMAZING! I think I went ONLY once at the main office for a simple question while Oakwood people were there.

The deer are coming in front of your balcony, everything you can wish for is just around the corner, the community is clean and the neighbors are nice and mostly filmmakers. Loved it, still do. That's why I kept returning here.

After 3 weeks of moving here in an unit under Avalon, there was a huge fire just next door and all the residents were very scared. 3 floors were on fire and my balcony was getting the flames from next door. The fire alarm started at around 11 pm, when the flames were already burning 3 apartments and the balconies around. That was really frightening. To see that the alarm starts after you're on fire. Basically, we just ran out, without taking anything, just thinking to save our lives. Everyone was screaming...it was hell. I spent the night in the car in pijamas and then in smoke, inside my apartment, without a door, as the firefighters broke it for protection.

I understood the fire was a misfortune event, but what happened afterwards, the management attitude towards it, the lack of respect...is outstanding. They replaced my door after one day with a broken one, that had a hole in it. I made a complaint about it and they came after 2 weeks and repaired the hole, but didn't change the door. It's even today dirty and scratched on the inside...

I lived for 2 months in a building that looked like a cave, without carpet, with black walls from the fire and with an unbearable smell of Smoke. It was like living in an underground that actually costs thousands of dollars.  I had to dry clean all my belongings twice to get the smoke smell out and asked management for help. They didn't care.

After that, they started construction, so I've lived until now...and it's still not finished...in a construction aria: without a ceiling, carpet, paint, anything, asbestos pieces outside my door, DANGER signs not to inhale or stand more time near it in the hallways, many many horrors... I told the management to be temporarily moved or to lower my rent for the months that I'm suffering these unexpected and unfortunate events, as it wasn't fair they're not doing anything and they're charging me for the luxury conditions I agreed on in the beginning. They didn't care. More than that, they told me that if I didn't like it I should move. I was treated horribly and I'm paying almost 1500$ for a studio without parking in these outrageous conditions.

I didn't want to give up my apartment and my beautiful living style there so hoped it would all come to an end. But no...it actually became worse. The water is shut off every other day and sometimes every day even for hours. 3 weeks ago I had to leave my house completely as there was no water at all for about 70 hours straight. 3 days without a drop of water...imagine that. It was a constant revolution in the community.

More than that, there is no parking space as they are blocking 3-4 parking lots that would fit tens and hundreds of cars for shooting sets every other week.

They basically have zero respect for the people that rent here now. Before, you could feel the Oakwood community spirit, but now you can only hear people complaining. I don't even have neighbors anymore. During the fire and construction site situation, I stopped seeing or hearing anyone around, except one neighbor. I think we're the only 2 people that decided to stay and wait for their life to be the same again in what it was before a beautiful community. I'm not even angry anymore I think. I'm over that. I'm just really sad for this total disrespect and for the fact that I'll have to move out when the lease is over if nothing is changing in a good way...and I don't want to. I want my Oakwood community back and I'm sure all the residents do.</review>< date>

< Text>
Toluca Hills is definitely a nice, comfortable place to live. We live in a studio, and they have done a great job of making it efficient, and feel spacious: Murphy bed, kitchen bar, built in dresser, etc. The walls are thick, so we ratherly ever hear our neighbors, aside from the loud beep from the keys when they enter their apartment; they are switching out these electronic keys with standard keys so that will not be a problem soon enough. They also do a nice job of taking care of their amenities, at least here on the South side. The pool and spa area are always clean. The workout room is small, but has enough equipment to get a decent workout. The theater room has a huge Samsung TV, with cable, and bluray player. The basketball and tennis courts are nice, and well kept most of the time. I think my favorite thing, overall, is that they have weekly activities for the residence: board game night, bingo night, cook outs, etc.

There are a few things that bother me though. First we living right next to Barham BLVD, and it's SO loud! When the doors closed, it reduces the sound, but you can still hear it. Several nights I have been woken up by a car peeling off at the stop light, and the flow is NEVER ENDING! I'm not sure if this is just an issue for this side, but given that the whole thing is surrounded by these busy roads, I would say it's not. Even when I am by the pool, I can hear the traffic. And if you're far enough away from the traffic, you'll more than likely hear people playing sports on the courts. So sound wise, not the greatest.

The amenities are excellent, and I really do appreciate them, and the effort put into keeping them clean, and working. My negative about this is that they can often be overcrowded, or reserved for events. This may not bother some, but for me it's an inconvience. Also, the south clubhouse is great, but I went to the north for Bingo and it seems run down, and outdated. The leasing office is in the south, so it's staffed well and better kept, and I would bet it's what they use to show of to future residents. For instance, the theater room in the north has a MUCH smaller, older television, the seats look worn, there was trash everywhere and there is a whole in the wall. Neither one has working surround sound, which was actually quite disappointing given its called a theater room, and they have speakers in the walls in ceiling just for design (and probably photographic) reasons.

I can't speak on most of the staff, as I haven't worked with many, but Rajeev, the gentleman handling our case has been excellent! I do feel, especially in the move in process there were some communication issues among the staff, as there are so many of them, but any time we talked to Rajeev he got things handled immediately!

Overall it's a great place to live! Everyone's friendly, it's within walking distance to a lot of things (including my school NYFA, which is a 30 minute walk), the amenities are nice, the activities are great, and the staff is very helpful. I put emphasize on the negatives because I feel it's only fair to let future residents know the downsides, so they don't feel cheated upon moving in. And as far as the inconviences go, they are definitely overshadowed by all the positives, including living in a gated community with 24hr security.<//Text>

1.) No bugs in apartment. I have an unfurnished so I can't speak for the furnished apartments, but I can say there are no bugs in my apartment and when I open the screen door I don't have to worry about spiders or ants coming in.

< Review>
Ultimately guests thought the venue was beautiful and food was good. Behind the scenes though I was sadly disappointed with their lack of responsiveness especially after we gave our final deposit. Really the final straw was when we were trying to arrange a time to get our cake toppers back. The coordinator swore up and down that she had them, then when we made the trip down all the way from San Francisco to pick them up they closed their offices even though they were supposed to be open and we had called the day prior to confirm we were coming. Luckily some cleaning staff was there and they were nice enough to search the kitchen and offices for the toppers (because again, the coordinator said they had them) but to no avail.

Even after that fiasco they said they would order us the same toppers and surprise, surprise they have been unresponsive again despite multiple tries to contact them.

Yes these are "just" cake toppers but I so rather them just say it my face from the start "whoops we threw out your 100 dollars cake toppers and we will not be replacing them for you" instead of this crazy run around.

Again, it seems like our experience is not that common so I don't know if I should take it personally or not. We are a simple couple! I don't think we asked for much or were difficult. We didn't even have the ceremony there or have weird demands. We even sprang for the extras like S'mores bar and tacos. I am still giving 3 stars because ultimately the wedding happened and guests left happy which is what we cared about. I'm just sad that I look back on my wedding day with a twinge of bitterness due to the post wedding ordeal.</Review>

<name>Kim B</name><Rate>1< /Rate>< review>
The front office staff were very nice, but that's the only good thing I can say about my experience here.  If you have a bird, forget about getting decent care here, but it's hard because there aren't many avian vets.   I contacted them for an appointment as soon as I saw my bird was ill.  I had to wait almost 4 business days (6 days total because of the weekend) to be seen because their avian vet apparently does not work Mondays.  My bird made it to his appointment, frankly because of my intensive care at home.  But when I got there, I had to wait in the cold reception area for 1/2 hour after my scheduled appointment time before we were called to a room.  But, luckily I know from many years of experience that sick birds need to be kept very warm, so I had a warming pad in the carrier for my bird and and kept it close to me to minimize the draft from the door opening and closing every few minutes.   They make you watch an avian care video prior to your arrival, and the vet tech that takes you to the room immediately gives you an avian care packet and starts talking to you about a pellet diet.  The vet came in shortly thereafter and he was very cold and unfriendly.  He did not ask me any questions whatsoever, but rather he immediately started lecturing me about needing to put the bird on a pellet diet.  Look, I am no stranger to birds.  I have had budgies and parrots all my life and they lived long lives.  My bird is on a very healthy diet and eats fresh veggies, grains, beans, egg whites with the shell, etc in addition to a high quality seed mix.  Despite me telling him about my extensive experience with birds, and telling him about my birds diet, and how I've been caring for him, the vet continued his preaching basically implying that the reason my bird was sick was because we weren't purchasing the pellet diet sold at his clinic.   So I became annoyed and told him that I don't need a lecture about the bird's diet,  that I have extensive experience with budgies, and his diet is not the reason he's sick because he became ill very suddenly and he was thriving beforehand.  He has the audacity to say, "No need to be upset!"    Then he switches gears and tells me about people leaving their birds in the cold and that's why they get an influx of sick birds at their clinic this time of year, all while he had my bird just sitting in a clear plastic box in the ice cold exam room. So I took it upon myself to put my bird back in his warm carrier and attempted to make the guy understand that this cannot be the reason my bird is sick because, again, I know not to do that and my bird has never been exposed to the cold.

I had to forcefully stress to this guy that it's not the bird's diet and being left in the cold, so he would open his mind to the possibility of something else, to which the vet simply said, "It could be anything."  Geeze.  Then I had to ask if there was any tests we could run.  He didn't even offer up any options we could possibly try.  He didn't want to do blood tests, to which I agree, the bird was too weak.  But then I had to ask if we could do tests on the bird's excrement to attempt to determine what was wrong, but frankly, he wasn't interested.  Basically, I got the feeling that he is already assuming my bird's a goner, and doesn't care to do anything for him.

So if you want an unfriendly vet that's not going to listen to you or even really examine or care about your bird, that will just make up his mind before you even walked in the door that your bird is sick because you aren't feeding them the pellet diet sold by his clinic, or that you must have neglected and left your bird out in the cold, and won't even talk to you about testing or treatment options, then this guy is for you.

At least my bird did come out of there with a better chance of surviving because they gave him a vitamin shot and antibiotics, and he did at least tell me to try baby bird feeding formula to help him get some nutrition.  Worth it, but I will be looking hard for another vet.<//review>

<Text>I took my English Bulldog; Sassy to Alta Rancho Pet Hospital for a second opinion on chronic problems she had been having with her skin.  I had been to 3 different vets over the previous 2 years in attempts to solve her problem with no success. She was suffering from a horrible odor an chronic itchiness around her bottom.  The odor was also coming from her face and ears.  We had tried all sorts of shampoos and rinses, oral drugs etc with no luck.
When I went to Alta Rancho Pet Hospital, I was greeted by a very friendly and knowledgeable staff. They took an exhaustive history of my dog's problems and then I got to meet Dr. Shufer.   We talked for a long time about what had been done in the past, what helped, what didn't help etc.  He did a very thorough exam of Sassy and discussed her problem with me, indicating that her issue was common to Bulldogs and related to chronic irritation from the skin folds creating an environment which allowed infection to occur. Because of her very tight corkscrew tail, and her generous facial folds, he suggested a surgical solution to Sassy's problem.  He warned me that it might seem radical, but that in the end, elimination of the folds was the only way to get sustained relief.  I thought over the concept for a few days and decided to go ahead with the surgery.
Dr. Shufer showed me their impressive surgical suite and described the procedure in detail.  Essentially, he was going to remove her tail entirely and cut away the facial folds to solve Sassy's problem.  The surgery went very smoothly as did the recovery.  2 weeks later, after the sutures were removed, my Sassy was totally fixed!  She stopped itching, stopped scooting and stopped stinking.  I don't want to sound extreme, but it was like a miracle.
I am so glad that we found Alta Rancho Pet Hospital and Dr. Shufer and I know Sassy is glad too.</Text>< pictures>

< review>
This place is consistently amazing. Been going here at least once a month and there hasn't been one time yet where I've thought "eh, I know they can do better." They set the bar for this style of food around the valley, as far as I'm concerned.

Definitely a great bang for your buck, regardless of whether you're getting their tacos, burritos, etc.  They keep their drink selections pretty well stocked too, so you'll usually find something you want.

Also, even with a line they manage to get through everyone relatively quick- I don't think I've ever waited more than ten minutes, tops. Most times I'm done within five.

TL;DR- do yourself a favor and check out the truck here at Corbin and Sherman Way! You won't regret it.< /review>

<Review>Whova is a pretty neat app. Our company used it for our national conference in 2019 and it really helped my plan out my agenda and network with other attendees. We decided to use the platform again this year for our virtual conference and I was surprised to see that it was still just as helpful! I loved that Whova is integrated with Zoom, without it I'm not sure if our conference would have been as successful. My only complaint is, I wish that I could still use the Zoom feature without leaving the Whova web portal. I found myself having to go back and forth between the Zoom app and the Whova portal during sessions which was challenging. We used the Whova portal's chat, poll, and Q&A feature which was important so that we could document responses but having to toggle between both applications was less than enjoyable. Despite that, I'd still recommend it.</Review>< Rating>
4</Rating>

<Resp>None<//Resp>< text>
I give this app 5 out of 5 stars. Whova brings together the ability to create an full-interactive shared conference experience by an organization. Creating an account is rather fun and easy. Whova streamlines the process for the attendee of keeping track of one's conference agenda, interests, community & social interactions, and more. It even give the opportunity to gamify the entire experience for opportunities to earn IRL or digital prizes by the Conference hosts. I so far thoroughly enjoy using this app as an attendee. The conference(s) I have attended intend to hopefully continue using Whova even after large in-person gatherings eventually resume for the purposes of allowing individuals to explore and experience more than can be done in-person but also to allow opportunity for those who cannot be there in-person. Keep up the good work Whova. *This is not a paid review. I am reviewing this from own experience.*< /text>

<UserId.>108970224983970144125<//UserId.><Name>Lisa Rothstein< /Name><Time>1593538485967</Time>< rating>
4<//rating>
<Review>I wasn't sure about Whova as it was a new platform to me, and my experience of other conference apps has been confusing, frustrating and just not a value-add. I just attended the IFVP conference (International Forum of Visual Practitioners) and I can say, Whova is different. Instead of just making people fill out a profile that no one reads, Whova truly facilitates the networking among participants by allowing topic discussions and virtual meetups. The content felt more like a "real" conference, with an easy-to-follow agenda. That said, there is a learning curve and some things could be improved. There is a bit of confusion between the mobile and desktop apps, especially when you receive emails full of links to content that when you click on them, it prompts you to download the mobile app (I have it already, i wanted the link to open in my browser). More attention should be paid to the desktop app now that most people are remote. The mobile app is more useful when a conference is F2F and the app is merely an enhancement, not the entire event. Also, Whova is not a substitute for smart humans running the event. We had several sessions that were better going directly to Zoom rather than through the Whova app and I appreciated receiving a clear email to that effect. Our moderators were up to speed and had a manned Zoom "help desk"as wells as clear instructions as to when the next session would be and how to join it. By the end of the day I loved Whova and look forward to the next two days of this conference (We have one in July and one in august) now that i'm familiar with the app.</Review><pics>None</pics>< response>

<gmapID>0x80dbff2fd018d491:0x9d9b1b5b6f49aa88</gmapID><text>Used this over the weekend of 13-15 December 2019 for a real estate conference.  It made it tremendously easy to meet others based on common interests and to engage in worthwhile conversations.

There were three things within the points system I would love to see improved upon.  I'm sure the intent of issuing points was to drive participation within the app, and it has succeeded at that.

1.  This year it seemed there were abundantly more "useless" posts/meet-ups being created solely for the sake of generating points.  Perhaps a point-reversal could be initiated if "x" number of participants don't subscribe within "x" number of hours?  And the points for those who "signed up" to go to that meet-up would also reversed.

2.  Many people were using multiple posts to explain a singular idea (ie: posting one sentence, or even one word, at a time).  Perhaps a tiered point system for posting messages/replies.  For example, a post of 1-100 characters generates 50 pts; a post of 101-200 characters generates 100pts; and so on...

3.  Lastly, I think the "Article Sharing" section was overused.

I gave more text to the negative side of this app, but this is a GREAT app and I will continue to use it in the future!<//text>< Pics>

<Name>Rick S<//Name>< Review>
I was at a conference that used this app and it was a great add to the overall meeting experience.  There was a lot of collaboration, folks reaching out to each other for meet-ups, starting group discussions, downloading silde presentations, etc.

This type of technology has been lacking in conference industry.  I downloaded app to my phone and tablet and it worked great on both.  Very functional and really easy to use!

One thing that was a little cumbersome was the conference had contests (person with most contributions, photos, blah blah) and some users contributed ALOT so that seemed to junk up some of the conversation threads that I was trying to follow.  Perhaps a way hide or flag to  unfollow something that isn't of interest as well as flag something that is?  Also, I was looking for different ways to search attendees.  It may have been disabled by the organizer, but I wanted to search for all attendees that were from a specific company or job title, etc.

Great conference and great app!!< /Review>

I just used WHOVA for the first time at an industry conference and I was so impressed with the platform. As a speaker, it gave me an opportunity to communicate in advance with my attendees and get them thinking about my topic, also an easy way to follow up. As an attendee, WHOVA provided a convenient way to connect with others, explore the agenda, and - BONUS - it linked directly with my calendar so I didn't miss anything! My only tiny complaint is that it sometimes sent duplicate messages, but that may have been a connectivity issue, and not related to the app (wi-fi was a bit spotty). Overall 5 stars!< /review>
